(metric tonnes)</th><td class="infobox-data">2,156,327</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;"><div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li>Source: <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> France<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Passenger Traffic &amp; Aircraft Movements<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</div> Freight Movements<sup id="cite_ref-AER_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AER-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">A\xc3\xa9roport de Paris-Charles-de-Gaulle</i>, <a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>CDG</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LFPG</b>), also known as <b>Roissy Airport</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_France" title="List of the busiest airports in France">largest international airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe"> busiest airports</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. Opened in 1974, it is located in <a href="/wiki/Roissy-en-France" title="Roissy-en-France">Roissy-en-France</a>, 23&#160;km (14&#160;mi) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. It is named after statesman <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> (1890\xe2\x80\x931970).\n</p><p>Charles de Gaulle Airport is located within portions of several <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">communes</a> in <a href="/wiki/Val-d%27Oise" title="Val-d&#39;Oise">Val-d\'Oise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seine-Saint-Denis" title="Seine-Saint-Denis">Seine-Saint-Denis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seine-et-Marne" title="Seine-et-Marne">Seine-et-Marne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It serves as the principal <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> and a destination for other legacy carriers (from <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> and <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a>), as well as a focus city for low-cost carriers <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vueling" title="Vueling">Vueling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a>. The Airport is operated by <a href="/wiki/Groupe_ADP" title="Groupe ADP">Groupe ADP</a> under the brand <a href="/wiki/Paris_A%C3%A9roport" title="Paris A\xc3\xa9roport">Paris A\xc3\xa9roport</a>.\n</p><p>In 2019, the airport handled 76,150,007 passengers and 498,175 aircraft movements,<sup id="cite_ref-pax_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pax-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> thus making it the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by passenger traffic">world\'s ninth busiest airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">Europe\'s second busiest</a> airport (after <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>) in terms of passenger numbers. Charles de Gaulle is also the busiest airport within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. In terms of cargo traffic, the airport is the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by cargo traffic">eleventh busiest in the world</a> and the busiest in Europe, handling 2,102,268 metric tonnes of cargo in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-pax_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pax-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2017, the airport offers direct flights to the most countries and hosts the most airlines in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Houalla" title="Marc Houalla">Marc Houalla</a> has been the director of the airport since 12 February 2018.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Statistics"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#See_also"><span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport covers 32.38 square kilometres (12.50&#160;sq&#160;mi) of land. The airport area, including terminals and runways, spans over three <i><a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">d\xc3\xa9partements</a></i> and six <i><a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">communes</a></i>:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Seine-et-Marne" title="Seine-et-Marne">Seine-et-Marne</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>: <a href="/wiki/Le_Mesnil-Amelot" title="Le Mesnil-Amelot">Le Mesnil-Amelot</a> (Terminal 2E, Satellites S3 and S4, and Terminal 2F), <a href="/wiki/Mauregard" title="Mauregard">Mauregard</a> (Terminals 1, 3), and <a href="/wiki/Mitry-Mory" title="Mitry-Mory">Mitry-Mory</a> (Terminal 2G) <i>communes</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-BEArep_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BEArep-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Seine-Saint-Denis" title="Seine-Saint-Denis">Seine-Saint-Denis</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>: <a href="/wiki/Tremblay-en-France" title="Tremblay-en-France">Tremblay-en-France</a> (Terminals 2A, 2B, 2C, 2D and Roissyp\xc3\xb4le) <i>commune</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-BEArep_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BEArep-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Val-d%27Oise" title="Val-d&#39;Oise">Val-d\'Oise</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>: <a href="/wiki/Roissy-en-France" title="Roissy-en-France">Roissy-en-France</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89piais-l%C3%A8s-Louvres" title="\xc3\x89piais-l\xc3\xa8s-Louvres">\xc3\x89piais-l\xc3\xa8s-Louvres</a> <i>communes</i>.</li></ul>\n<p>The choice of constructing an international aviation hub outside of central Paris was made due to a limited prospect of potential relocations or expropriations and the possibility of further expanding the airport in the future.\n</p><p>Management of the airport lies solely on the authority of <i><a href="/wiki/Groupe_ADP" title="Groupe ADP">Groupe ADP</a></i>, which also manages <a href="/wiki/Orly_Airport" title="Orly Airport">Orly</a> (south of Paris), <a href="/wiki/Paris_%E2%80%93_Le_Bourget_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris \xe2\x80\x93 Le Bourget Airport">Le Bourget</a> (to the immediate southwest of Charles de Gaulle Airport, now used for general aviation and Paris Air Shows), several smaller airfields in the suburbs of Paris, and other airports directly or indirectly worldwide.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The planning and construction phase of what was known then as <i>A\xc3\xa9roport de Paris Nord</i> (Paris North Airport)<sup id="cite_ref-charlesdegaulleairport.co.uk_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charlesdegaulleairport.co.uk-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> began in 1966. On 8 March 1974 the airport, renamed Charles de Gaulle Airport, opened. Terminal 1 was built in an <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> design of a ten-floors-high circular building surrounded by seven satellite buildings, each with six gates allowing sunlight to enter through <a href="/wiki/Apertures" class="mw-redirect" title="Apertures">apertures</a>. The main architect was <a href="/wiki/Paul_Andreu" title="Paul Andreu">Paul Andreu</a>, who was also in charge of the extensions during the following decades.\n</p><p>Following the introduction of the brand <a href="/wiki/Paris_A%C3%A9roport" title="Paris A\xc3\xa9roport">Paris A\xc3\xa9roport</a> to all its Parisian airports, <a href="/wiki/Groupe_ADP" title="Groupe ADP">Groupe ADP</a> also announced major changes for the Charles de Gaulle Airport: Terminals of the Satellite 1 will be merged, as well as terminals 2B and 2D. A new luggage automated <a href="/wiki/Sorter_(logistics)" title="Sorter (logistics)">sorting system</a> and conveyor under Terminal 2E Hall L was installed to speed luggage delivery time for airlines operating Paris-Charles de Gaulle\'s hub. The <a href="/wiki/CDG_Express" title="CDG Express">CDG Express</a>, the direct express rail link from Paris to Charles de Gaulle Airport, is planned for completion by 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_identity">Corporate identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Corporate identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Frutiger_(typeface)" title="Frutiger (typeface)">Frutiger typeface</a> was commissioned for use in the airport and implemented on signs throughout the building in 1975. Initially called <i>Roissy</i>, it was renamed after its designer <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Frutiger" title="Adrian Frutiger">Adrian Frutiger</a>.\n</p><p>Until 2005, every <a href="/wiki/Public_address" class="mw-redirect" title="Public address">PA announcement</a> made at Terminal 1 was preceded by a distinctive chime, nicknamed "Indicatif Roissy" and composed by <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Parmegiani" title="Bernard Parmegiani">Bernard Parmegiani</a> in 1971. The chime can be heard in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Polanski" title="Roman Polanski">Roman Polanski</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Frantic_(film)" title="Frantic (film)">Frantic</a></i>. The chime was officially replaced by the "Indicatif ADP" chime.\n</p><p>On 14 April 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Groupe_ADP" title="Groupe ADP">Groupe ADP</a> rolled out the <i>Connect 2020</i> corporate strategy and the commercial brand <a href="/wiki/Paris_A%C3%A9roport" title="Paris A\xc3\xa9roport">Paris A\xc3\xa9roport</a> was applied to all Parisian airports, including Le Bourget airport.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LFPG_Layout.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/LFPG_Layout.svg/220px-LFPG_Layout.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/LFPG_Layout.svg/330px-LFPG_Layout.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/LFPG_Layout.svg/440px-LFPG_Layout.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="1063" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LFPG_Layout.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airport Diagram</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg/220px-Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg/330px-Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg/440px-Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Terminal 1 (before refurbishment)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CDG-aerialview.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/CDG-aerialview.jpg/220px-CDG-aerialview.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/CDG-aerialview.jpg/330px-CDG-aerialview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/CDG-aerialview.jpg/440px-CDG-aerialview.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CDG-aerialview.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Terminal 2A and 2B (before refurbishment)</div></div></div>\n<p>Charles de Gaulle Airport has three terminals: Terminal 1 is the oldest and situated opposite to Terminal 3; Terminal 2 is located at another side with 7 sub-terminal buildings (2A to 2G). Terminal 2 was originally built exclusively for <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-charlesdegaulleairport.co.uk_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charlesdegaulleairport.co.uk-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> since then it has been expanded significantly and now also hosts other airlines. Terminals 2A to 2F are interconnected by elevated walkways and situated next to each other. Terminal 2G is a satellite building connected by shuttle bus.<sup id="cite_ref-charlesdegaulleairport.co.uk_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charlesdegaulleairport.co.uk-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal 3 (formerly known as "Terminal 9") hosts charter and low-cost airlines. The <a href="/wiki/CDGVAL" title="CDGVAL">CDGVAL</a> light-rail shuttle connects Terminal 2 to Terminals 1/3 and their parking lots. Refer to <b>Ground Transportation</b> below for inter-terminal transfers and transport to central Paris.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first terminal, designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Andreu" title="Paul Andreu">Paul Andreu</a>, was built in the image of an <a href="/wiki/Octopus" title="Octopus">octopus</a>. It consists of a circular terminal building which houses key functions such as check-in counters and baggage claim conveyors. Seven satellites with boarding gates are connected to the central building by underground walkways.\n</p><p>The central building, with a large skylight in its centre, dedicates each floor to a single function. The first floor is reserved for technical operations and not accessible to the public. The second floor contains shops and restaurants, the CDGVAL inter-terminal shuttle train platforms (for Terminal 2 and trains to central Paris) and check-in counters from a recent renovation. The majority of check-in counters, however, are located on the third floor, which also has access to taxi stands, bus stops and special pick-up vehicles. Departing passengers with valid boarding passes can reach the fourth floor, which houses duty-free stores and border control posts, for the boarding gates. The fifth floor contains baggage claim conveyors for arriving passengers. All four upper floors have assigned areas for parking and airline offices.\n</p><p>Passages between the third, fourth and fifth floors are provided by a tangle of escalators arranged through the centre of the building. These escalators are suspended over the central court. Each escalator is covered with a transparent tube to shelter from all weather conditions. These escalators were often used in film shootings (e.g. <i>The Last Gang of Ariel Zeitoun</i>). The <a href="/wiki/Alan_Parsons_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Alan Parsons Project">Alan Parsons Project</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/I_Robot_(album)" title="I Robot (album)">I Robot</a></i> features these escalators on its cover.\n</p><p>Terminal 1 is used by mainly <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> members except those who operate from Terminal 2.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 2 is spread across seven sub-terminals: 2A to 2G. Terminals 2A to 2F are connected by inter-terminal walkways, but Terminal 2G is a satellite building 800&#160;m (0.5&#160;mi) away. Terminal 2G can only be accessed by shuttle bus from Terminals 1, 2A to 2F and 3. The CDGVAL inter-terminal shuttle train, Paris RER Regional-Express and high-speed TGV rail station, <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_2_TGV" title="A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV">A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV</a>, is located within the Terminal 2 complex and between 2C and 2E (on one side) or 2D and 2F (on the opposite side).\n</p><p>Terminal 2F was used for the filming of the music video for the <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Day" title="Beautiful Day">Beautiful Day</a>". The band also had their picture taken inside Terminal 2F for the album artwork of their 2000 album <i><a href="/wiki/All_That_You_Can%27t_Leave_Behind" title="All That You Can&#39;t Leave Behind">All That You Can\'t Leave Behind</a></i>.\n</p><p>Terminal 2 is used by <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, all <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> and  <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> airlines, some <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> members (most operate from Terminal 1) and other airlines.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Collapse_of_Terminal_2E">Collapse of Terminal 2E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Collapse of Terminal 2E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png/220px-Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png/330px-Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png/440px-Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png 2x" data-file-width="485" data-file-height="389" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Collapsed Terminal 2E, June 2004</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg/220px-Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="74" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg/330px-Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg/440px-Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4384" data-file-height="1484" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_plan_Roissy_CDG_Terminal_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of terminal 2 various halls</div></div></div>\n<p>On 23 May 2004, shortly after the inauguration of terminal 2E, a portion of it collapsed near <a href="/wiki/Gate_(airport)" title="Gate (airport)">Gate</a> E50, killing four people.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Two of the dead were reported to be Chinese citizens, one Czech and the other Lebanese.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Three other people were injured in the collapse. Terminal 2E had been inaugurated in 2003 after some delays in construction and was designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Andreu" title="Paul Andreu">Paul Andreu</a>. Administrative and judicial enquiries were started. Andreu also designed Terminal 3 at <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai International Airport</a>, which collapsed while under construction on 28 September 2004.\n</p><p>Before this accident, ADP had been planning for an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in 2005 with the new terminal as a major attraction for investors. The partial collapse and indefinite closing of the terminal just before the beginning of summer seriously hurt the airport\'s business plan.\n</p><p>In February 2005, the results from the administrative inquiry were published. The experts pointed out that there was no single fault, but rather a number of causes for the collapse, in a design that had little margin for safety. The inquiry found the concrete <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">vaulted roof</a> was not resilient enough and had been pierced by metallic pillars and some openings weakened the structure. Sources close to the inquiry also disclosed that the whole building chain had worked as close to the limits as possible, so as to reduce costs. Paul Andreu denounced the building companies for having not correctly prepared the <a href="/wiki/Reinforced_concrete" title="Reinforced concrete">reinforced concrete</a>.\n</p><p>On 17 March 2005, ADP decided to tear down and rebuild the whole part of Terminal 2E (the "jetty") of which a section had collapsed, at a cost of approximately \xe2\x82\xac100&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The reconstruction replaced the innovative concrete tube style of the jetty with a more traditional steel and glass structure. During reconstruction, two temporary departure lounges were constructed in the vicinity of the terminal that replicated the capacity of 2E before the collapse. The terminal reopened completely on 30 March 2008.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2G">Terminal 2G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terminal 2G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg/220px-Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg/330px-Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg/440px-Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2, former display screen</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_France_A320s_(F-GTAM,_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH)_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Air_France_A320s_%28F-GTAM%2C_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH%29_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg/220px-Air_France_A320s_%28F-GTAM%2C_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH%29_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Air_France_A320s_%28F-GTAM%2C_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH%29_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg/330px-Air_France_A320s_%28F-GTAM%2C_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH%29_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Air_France_A320s_%28F-GTAM%2C_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH%29_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg/440px-Air_France_A320s_%28F-GTAM%2C_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH%29_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_France_A320s_(F-GTAM,_F-GTAL_and_F-GKXH)_at_Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> aircraft on stands at Terminal 2F at Charles de Gaulle Airport.</div></div></div>\n<p>Terminal 2G, dedicated to regional Air France and <a href="/wiki/HOP!" class="mw-redirect" title="HOP!">HOP!</a> flights and its affiliates, opened in 2008. This terminal is to the east of all terminals and can only be reached by shuttle bus. Terminal 2G is used for passengers flying in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> (and thus has no passport control) and handles Air France regional and European traffic and provides small-capacity planes (up to 150 passengers) with a faster turnaround time than is currently possible by enabling them to park close to the new terminal building and boarding passengers primarily by bus, or walking. A bus line called "navette orange" connects the terminal 2G inside the security check area with terminals 2E and 2F. Passengers transferring to other terminals need to continue their trip with other bus shuttles within the security check area if they do not need to get their bags.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_2E_Hall_L_.28Satellite_3.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2E_Hall_L_(Satellite_3)">Terminal 2E Hall L (Satellite 3)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Terminal 2E Hall L (Satellite 3)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The completion of 750&#160;m (2,460&#160;ft) long Satellite 3 (or S3) to the immediate east of Terminals 2E and 2F provides further <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jetways</a> for large-capacity airliners, specifically the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>. Check-in and <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">baggage handling</a> are provided by the existing infrastructure in Terminals 2E and 2F. Satellite 3 was opened in part on 27 June 2007 and fully operational in September 2007. It corresponds now to gates L of terminal 2E.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_2E_Hall_M_.28Satellite_4.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2E_Hall_M_(Satellite_4)">Terminal 2E Hall M (Satellite 4)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Terminal 2E Hall M (Satellite 4)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The satellite S4, adjacent to the S3 and part of terminal 2E, officially opened on 28 June 2012. It corresponds now to gates M of terminal 2E. Dedicated to long-haul flights, it has the ability to handle 16 aircraft at the same time, with an expected capacity of 7.8 million passengers per year. Its opening has led to the relocation of all SkyTeam airlines to terminals 2E (for international carriers), 2F (for Schengen European carriers) and 2G.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Air France has moved all of its operations previously located at 2C to 2E. In October 2012, 2F closed its international operations and became completely Schengen, allowing for all Air France flights currently operating in 2D to relocate to terminal 2F. Further, in April 2013, Terminal 2B closed for a complete renovation (all airlines relocated to 2D) and will receive upgrades including the addition of a second floor completely dedicated to arrivals. Once 2B is completed, 2D will close and receive similar upgrades, including the addition of a new floor. Low-cost carrier easyJet has shown its interest in being the sole carrier at 2B.<sup id="cite_ref-S4_ADP_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S4_ADP-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> To facilitate connections, a new boarding area between 2A and 2C was opened in March 2012. It allows for all security and passport control to be handled in a single area, allows for many new shopping opportunities as well as new airline lounges, and eases transfer restrictions between 2A and 2C.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cancelled_project_for_Terminal_4">Cancelled project for Terminal 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Cancelled project for Terminal 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/La_Tribune" title="La Tribune">La Tribune</a></i>, a new Terminal 4 is likely to be built around 2025, when Charles de Gaulle Airport\'s maximum capacity of 80 million will be reached. This new Terminal 4, when constructed, will be able to accommodate 30\xe2\x80\x9340 million passengers per year and will most likely be built north of Terminal 2E.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The Terminal 4 proposal was cancelled in 2021, after reduced traffic from the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> and new environmental regulations made it unfeasible.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3">Terminal 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terminal 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 3 is located 1&#160;km (0.62&#160;mi) away from Terminal 1. It consists of one single building for arrivals and departures. The walking distance between Terminals 1 and 3 is 3&#160;km (1.9&#160;mi) long, however, the rail station (named as "CDG Airport Terminal 1") for RER and CDGVAL trains are only at a distance of 300&#160;m (980&#160;ft). Terminal 3 has no boarding gates constructed and all passengers are ferried via boarding buses to the aircraft stands.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Roissyp.C3.B4le"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Roissyp\xc3\xb4le">Roissyp\xc3\xb4le</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Roissyp\xc3\xb4le">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Roissyp\xc3\xb4le is a complex consisting of office buildings, shopping areas, hotels, and a bus coach and RER B station within Charles de Gaulle Airport. The complex includes the head office of Air France,<sup id="cite_ref-GEMO_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEMO-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Continental_Square" title="Continental Square">Continental Square</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilton Hotels">Hilton</a> Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and le D\xc3\xb4me building. Le D\xc3\xb4me includes the head office of Air France Consulting, an Air France subsidiary.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Continental Square has the head office of Air France subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Servair" title="Servair">Servair</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and the Air France Vaccinations Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a station of <i>A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV</i></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gare_CDG_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Gare_CDG_2.JPG/220px-Gare_CDG_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Gare_CDG_2.JPG/330px-Gare_CDG_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Gare_CDG_2.JPG/440px-Gare_CDG_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gare_CDG_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Train station of <i>A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV</i></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CDGVAL">CDGVAL</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: CDGVAL">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport\'s terminals are served by a free automated shuttle rail system, consisting of two lines (<a href="/wiki/CDGVAL" title="CDGVAL">CDGVAL</a> and LISA). \n</p><p>CDGVAL (<i>Charles de Gaulle V\xc3\xa9hicule Automatique L\xc3\xa9ger</i>, English: <i>Charles de Gaulle light automatic vehicle</i>) links Terminal 1, parking lot PR, <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_1_(Paris_RER)" title="A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 1 (Paris RER)">A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 1</a> RER station (located inside Roissyp\xc3\xb4le and next to Terminal 3), Parking lot PX, and the <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_2_TGV" title="A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV">A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV</a> and RER station located between Terminals 2C, 2D, 2E, and 2F\n</p><p>LISA (<i>Liaison Interne Satellite A\xc3\xa9rogare,</i> English: <i>Connection internal satellite terminal)</i> links Terminal 2E to the Satellite S3 (L Gates) and Satellite S4 (M Gates).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RER">RER</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: RER">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Charles de Gaulle Airport is connected to central Paris by the <a href="/wiki/RER_B" title="RER B">RER B</a>, a hybrid <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">suburban commuter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> line. The service has two stations on the airport grounds:<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_1_(Paris_RER)" title="A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 1 (Paris RER)">A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 1</a> station, located inside Roissyp\xc3\xb4le and next to Terminal 3. The station provides the fastest access to Terminal 1 via a connection on CDGVAL.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_2_TGV" title="A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV">A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV</a> station, located between Terminals 2C, 2D, 2E, and 2F.</li></ul>\n<p>During most times, there are two types of services that operate on the RER B between Charles de Gaulle airport and Paris:\n</p>\n<ul><li>4 trains per hour making all stops between Charles de Gaulle airport and <a href="/wiki/Saint-R%C3%A9my-l%C3%A8s-Chevreuse_(Paris_RER)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint-R\xc3\xa9my-l\xc3\xa8s-Chevreuse (Paris RER)">Saint-R\xc3\xa9my-l\xc3\xa8s-Chevreuse</a></li>\n<li>4 trains per hour that offer non-stop express service between Charles de Gaulle airport and <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a> and then all all stops to <a href="/wiki/Massy-Palaiseau_station" title="Massy-Palaiseau station">Massy\xe2\x80\x93Palaiseau</a></li></ul>\n<p>The express RER B service only stops at the Terminal 1 (also for Terminal 3) and Terminal 2 stations before Gare du Nord. Journey time is 30\xe2\x80\x9335 minutes. The all-stops RER B service takes about 35\xe2\x80\x9340 minutes and is sometimes overtaken by the express RER B trains.\n</p><p>The RER B has historically suffered from slowness and overcrowding, so French authorities are building <a href="/wiki/CDG_Express" title="CDG Express">CDG Express</a>, a train service that will operate non-stop from Charles de Gaulle Airport to Paris <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_l%27Est" title="Gare de l&#39;Est">Gare de l\'Est</a> railway station (next to Gare du Nord) starting in 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TGV">TGV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: TGV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 2 includes a <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_2_TGV" title="A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV">TGV station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/LGV_Interconnexion_Est" title="LGV Interconnexion Est">LGV Interconnexion Est</a> line. <a href="/wiki/TGV_inOui" title="TGV inOui">TGV inOui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouigo" title="Ouigo">Ouigo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> high-speed services operate from the station offering services to stations across France and into Belgium and The Netherlands.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/RATP_Bus_Network#Airport_Direct_Shuttle_Buses" class="mw-redirect" title="RATP Bus Network">Roissybus</a> offers non-stop express service between <a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ra_(Paris_M%C3%A9tro)" title="Op\xc3\xa9ra (Paris M\xc3\xa9tro)">Op\xc3\xa9ra</a> station of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_M%C3%A9tro" title="Paris M\xc3\xa9tro">Paris M\xc3\xa9tro</a> and Charles de Gaulle airport, making stops all terminals (except 2G).</li>\n<li>"Magical Shuttle" offers non-stop express service between <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Paris" title="Disneyland Paris">Disneyland Paris</a> and Charles de Gaulle airport, making stops at Terminal 1 and Terminal 2E/2F.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/RATP_Bus_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="RATP Bus Network">RATP bus</a> 350 offers local (all-stops) service between <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_l%27Est" title="Gare de l&#39;Est">Gare de l\'Est</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a> in Paris and Charles de Gaulle airport, all terminals (except 2G) and other areas of the airport.</li>\n<li>RATP bus 351 offers local service between <a href="/wiki/Nation_(Paris_M%C3%A9tro_and_RER)" title="Nation (Paris M\xc3\xa9tro and RER)">Nation</a> station in Paris, the <a href="/wiki/Eurolines" title="Eurolines">Eurolines</a> station at <a href="/wiki/Gallieni_(Paris_M%C3%A9tro)" title="Gallieni (Paris M\xc3\xa9tro)">Gallieni</a> station, all terminals (except 2G) and other areas of the airport.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Noctilien" title="Noctilien">Noctilien</a> routes N140 and N143 offers local service during the overnight hours between Gare de l\'Est/Gare du Nord in Paris and Charles de Gaulle airport, all terminals (except 2G) and other areas of the airport.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Long-distance_bus">Long-distance bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Long-distance bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/BlaBlaBus" title="BlaBlaBus">BlaBlaBus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurolines" title="Eurolines">Eurolines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Flixbus" title="Flixbus">Flixbus</a> all offer services to international and domestic destinations from the bus station outside of the <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_1_(Paris_RER)" title="A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 1 (Paris RER)">A\xc3\xa9roport Charles de Gaulle 1</a> RER station.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car">Car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Charles de Gaulle Airport is directly connected to <a href="/wiki/Autoroute_A1_(France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Autoroute A1 (France)">Autoroute A1</a> which connects Paris and Lille.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_airports">Alternative airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Alternative airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The two other airports serving Paris are <a href="/wiki/Orly_Airport" title="Orly Airport">Orly Airport</a> (south of Paris, the other major airport in Paris) and <a href="/wiki/Le_Bourget_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Le Bourget Airport">Le Bourget Airport</a> (for <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business_jet" title="Business jet">private jets</a>).\n</p><p>Several <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airlines</a> also advertise <a href="/wiki/Beauvais%E2%80%93Till%C3%A9_Airport" title="Beauvais\xe2\x80\x93Till\xc3\xa9 Airport">Beauvais\xe2\x80\x93Till\xc3\xa9 Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2lons_Vatry_Airport" title="Ch\xc3\xa2lons Vatry Airport">Ch\xc3\xa2lons Vatry Airport</a>, respectively 85 kilometres (53&#160;mi) and 165 kilometres (103&#160;mi) from Paris proper, as serving "Paris" with <i>Paris\xe2\x80\x93Beauvais</i> and <i>Paris\xe2\x80\x93Vatry</i>. Beauvais airport has no railway connections, but there is a shuttle bus to central Paris 15 times daily.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 6 January 1993, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cityline_Flight_5634" class="mw-redirect" title="Lufthansa Cityline Flight 5634">Lufthansa Flight 5634</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a> to Paris, which was carried out under the <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_CityLine" title="Lufthansa CityLine">Lufthansa CityLine</a> brand using a Contact Air <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Dash_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Dash 8">Dash 8-300</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registered</a> D-BEAT), hit the ground 1,800 metres (5,900&#160;ft) short of the runway of Charles de Gaulle Airport, resulting in the death of four out of the 23 passengers on board. The four crew members survived. The accident occurred after the pilot had to abort the <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">final approach</a> to the airport because the runway had been closed: the aircraft immediately ahead, a <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a>, had suffered a blown tire upon landing.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 25 July 2000, a <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">Air France Flight 4590</a> from Charles de Gaulle to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> in New York, crashed into Les Relais Bleus Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Gonesse" title="Gonesse">Gonesse</a>, killing everyone on the aircraft and four people on the ground. Investigations concluded that a tire burst during take-off roll, after running over a metal strip on the runway that had detached from a <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10-30">McDonnell Douglas DC-10-30</a> which departed shortly before, leading to a ruptured fuel tank and resulting in engine failure and other damage. Concorde was conducting a charter flight for a German tour company.</li>\n<li>On 25 May 2001, a freight-carrying <a href="/wiki/Short_360" title="Short 360">Short SH36</a> (operated as Streamline flight 200), departing to <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a>, England, collided on the runway with departing <a href="/wiki/Air_Libert%C3%A9" title="Air Libert\xc3\xa9">Air Libert\xc3\xa9</a> flight 8807, an <a href="/wiki/MD-83" class="mw-redirect" title="MD-83">MD-83</a> jet. The first officer of the SH36 was killed when the wing tip of the MD-83 tore through his side of the flight deck. The captain was slightly injured and all others aboard survived.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a Wikidata query and sources</a>.</small>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CDG_Destinations.svg" class="image"><img alt="" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CDG_Destinations.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries served by CDG</div></div></div>\n<p>The following table shows total passenger numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table
